Shabbat Torah Readers

Scott Zimmerman Coordinator

Torah is at the foundation of
the Jewish people. It records our ear-
liest history; it outlines fundamen-
tal laws; it models significant values
and standards of behavior; it reflects
basic truths about human nature; it
opens us to relationships with, and
wonder of, the divine. Its language
is the portal to Jewish study, worship,
and identity.

Of all the outstanding areas
in which the Jacksonville Jewish
Center has excelled, we have been
most fortunate in being blessed with
people who have made their talents
meaningful to the congregation and
a source of recognition and pride
throughout the Southeast. The num-
bers of students and lay people who
can be depended upon to read Torah
is an outstanding accomplishment
for us to be proud of and very hard
for other synagogues to match. This
is a direct reflection of the leader-
ship of Ted Gross and his commit-
ment to educational excellence in our
schools and the dedication of our
Torah readers and our teachers. Iam
very proud to be associated with the
Torah reading program and the high
level of participation we have
achieved. The commitment and en-
couragement of our synagogue lead-
ers and organizations will ensure that
this high quality will be maintained
for future generations to come.
I would like to thank Ted Gross for
his guidance and encouragement as
well as all of our readers and teach-
ers for their continued support and
cooperation and wish you all a heart-
felt Mazel Tov.

The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs

 

 

Jacksonville
Jewish Center

Centennial
Celebration
1901 = A(O)OAl
ed

os As our educational institution enters a new year with all its anticipations
and promises, one would be remiss not to examine the preparation necessary for our
future endeavors. Our movements forward are not isolated events, but represent the

combined efforts of our lay leadership, parents, PTA, and Center professional staff.

Solomon Schechter Day School

Both our General Studies and Judaic curriculums have undergone scrutiny
by our own dedicated professional staff and the Florida Council of Independent
Schools. Our General Studies Program received ten Special Commendations relating
to our staff, Facility, and students. We met or exceeded our standards established by
the organization on a state level and received our renewed five-year Accreditation.

We added the position of Judaic Studies Curriculum Coordinator with the
purpose of continued improvement in this vital area of our school.

The successful Tal-Am and Tal-Sela Programs of Hebrew language
development are now fully implemented throughout the elementary grades.

 

Willard M. Kennedy Our Middle School has undergone some important changes to prepare for

Principal the addition of the eighth grade to complete our concept of a fully operational

educational program for this age. With the funding supplied by the IPO and Samuel

and Esther Galinsky endowment, the addition of a state-of-the-art Science Lab will be completed. Combined with the expansion

and improvements of our computer instructional program this past year, we offer educational experiences and preparation that
meet or exceed other programs in our community.

The school has made a commitment to provide competent staffing of our program and has obtained ten staff members
with a Masters Degree. In addition, educational in-service programs are made available on a regular basis.

Strengthened by a commitment to constantly reassess, improve and surpass our previous achievement, we will keep
our school a stronghold for the acquisition of knowledge and the transmission of the Jewish soul to yet another generation.

- Williard M. Kennedy

Dear Friends and Fellow Members:

As we enter our fourth year in Jacksonville, our family has many blessings for which
to be thankful. Without exception, our involvement in the JJC has been the
cornerstone of our social, philanthropic, business and ritual growth in this community
we are so proud to call home.

We are humbled by the contributions we see our dear friends make, and the
leadership positions they accept in an effort to further improve our great institutions
and annual events. We are grateful for having been provided opportunities to
contribute and really “make a difference” as we support our community leaders.

In 1997, Suzi and | moved to Jacksonville in hopes of improving our business and
melding with a community that would foster the development of our young family.
Little did we know the impact on our own development, or the base of social and
business friends that The JJC and our wonderful community would have. It has
been nothing short of amazing!

As you look at the back cover, which we are very proud to have supported since we
arrived and have committed to support for the next three years, you will see a new
name. “Wheaton” has replaced “Bekins” as the van line with which our local company
will be affiliated. We are very proud to have secured this new affiliation and to be
able to provide you and your family with the consistency our local company has worked
hard to deliver; and with the support of the most stable and well regarded van line in
the country.

Wheaton has been recognized for their leadership in support of Henri Landwerth’s
organization, “Give Kids the World”. They have also been consistently awarded the
Good Housekeeping seal of approval and have been rated # 1 for service and value
by Consumer Reports Magazine. As Wheaton’s largest domestic and international
affiliate, we are proud to have aligned ourselves with a group that has demonstrated
the integrity and ‘commitment to community’ that Wheaton has.

Celebrating the “Crown Moving Systems” name, we will continue to provide attributes
of “Crystal Service” to the valued clients and friends we serve. Whether its moving
our new rabbi to Jacksonville, or helping you move down the block, please know that
our continuing commitment will be toward delivering the highest quality and best-
valued moving services available.

We look forward to our future as members of the congregation and responsible
participants in our community’s efforts to further strengthen and grow the JJC and
all it represents. |

L’Shana Tovah!
MIcHAEL Weiss

Committees

 

Adult Education

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial

Celebration
1901 - 2007
ae Sa

Learning never stops at the Center. From the smallest of
our members, well into adulthood, people are studying at the
cuter

This year the adult education committee, chaired by Etta
Drashin, coordinated a wide variety of classes.

As the synagogue is still the center of Jewish communal
life, a Jew who can’t read Hebrew must feel peripheral in the midst
of the religion’s core institution. For a Jew who can’t read Hebrew,
a synagogue Service is a spectator sport. To help those congregants
who never learned to read Hebrew, or who have forgotten what
they learned as a child, beginner’s Hebrew was taught by Arlene
Yegelwel and Etta Drashin.

 

Rabbi Gaffney and Professor Stephen Berk
Shabbaton Speaker

Other classes were taught to those who already knew how
to read Hebrew, but wanted to stretch their knowledge even further.
Cantor Aron Heller led a Shabbat Learner’s Minyan, which walked the students through the Saturday morning liturgy. Later
in the year, Larry Bernard gave lessons in Haftorah trope.

Rabbi David Gaffney led a series of lectures titled “Judaism for the Skeptic” that ran on six Wednesday nights over the
course of the year. The series was very well attended and the following issues were discussed: (1)Where is God? (2) Does
Prayer Work? (3) The Bible Notes “and God said” did He really say? (4) The Chosen People, Are we really chosen? (5) Why
did this Happen to Me, and (6) Why Should I be Religious?

The annual Marilyn and Louis Safer Shabbaton featured Professor Stephen M. Berk as the Scholar in residence.
Professor Berk, who is a professor at Union College in Schenectady, New York, was an absolutely superb lecturer. His lectures
included The Jewish State and the Struggle to Have a Jewish Soul, The American-Jewish Experience, and The Incredible First
Century. |

Saturdays after services, Rabbi Gaffney led his Torah Study, informal discussions in various family’s homes on a
monthly basis. Topics which included such things as “ Do We Fight for the Temple Mount?” (shortly after Sharon’s visit which
set off violence throughout the State of Israel) and ““ How Far Do We Reach out to Non-Jews?”

Sisterhood sponsored three book reviews and the Men’s Club taught members how to lay tefillin, which was a followed
by the World Wide Wrap on Sunday, January 28.

Family University, under the direction of Pam Maman and the Solomon Schechter Day School, provided a unique
opportunity for members of the community to attend classes on the Jewish Life Cycle.

On alternate Sunday mornings, Rabbi Gaffney led several congregants in a Talmud study. These classes provided
much information on how our prayer service came about. The background information
that the rabbi provided was very helpful.

On the mornings that Rabbi Gaffney taught the Talmud class, he continued teaching
and taught “An Introduction to Judaism” class, for adults that wanted to learn more
about their heritage and to those who were considering conversion to Judaism.

On the evening of March 12, Dr. Ismar Schorsch, Chancellor of the Jewish
Theological Seminary offered his reflections on the accomplishments of Conservative
Judaism and his projections for the future of American Jewry from his vantage point
as the leader of the Conservative Movement. Chancellor Schorsch’s visit to Jacksonville
was the first that any chancellor has made to North Florida.

Philip Pakula led Firing Line, a discussion format on the crucial issues of the day.
Joan Levin instructed Israeli dancing on Monday nights, and Stella Finck gave lessons
on how to make challah from scratch.

 

Elissa Vinning, Carol Weinstein
make Challah from Scratch

The Jacksonville Jewish Federation
serves as a central resource for our Jewish
community. In summary, the Federation
is dedicated to providing for the welfare
of every Jewish person living in
Jacksonville. Through a partnership with
the United Jewish Communities, formerly
known as UJA, we are equally committed
to the survival of, and quality of life for,
every Jew living in Israel and throughout
the Diaspora.

The five major local recipient
agencies of funds raised by the
Federation are the Jewish Community
Alliance, Jewish Family & Community
Services, River Garden Hebrew Home,
Jacksonville Jewish Foundation and the
Solomon Schechter Day School. We are
proud of the invaluable services provided
by these five outstanding Jewish agencies.
It is a privilege to assist them in trying to
meet their goals.

Executive Director
Paulette Keifer

Board of Trustees
Melvin Gottlieb, President
Michael Donziger* Michael DuBow
Jeff Edwards Gloria Einstein
Melvyn Fruit Mark Green
Arthur Hurwitz Barbara Jaffe
Howard Korman Joan Levin
Neil Presser Michael Schneider
Steve Sherman Mark Shorstein

Community Agencies

Jacksonville Jewish Federation

8505 San Jose Blvd. Jacksonville, FL 32217
448-5000 Fax.- 448-5715 * www.jaxjewish.org

Jewish education is extremely
important, and the Federation is proud to
support the Solomon Schechter Day
School, Beit Midrash and Etz Chaim
Hebrew Academy. Through the Joan Levin
Gift of Israel program, Federation is
helping to make the dream of a trip to Israel
a reality for Jewish teens in our community.

The Federation is involved with
community relations, leadership
development and Missions to Israel. We
will continue to work in cooperation with
our local agencies, UJC and the synagogues
to address the vital issues and challenges
in the entire arena of Jewish continuity.

Our Board wishes members of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center a Happy and
Healthy New Year.

— Mitchell Levine, Md, President
—Alan Margolies, Executive Director

< Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
“aie

The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation is dedicated to accumulating permanent
assets which can provide a source of income to help support the stability and
continuity of the Agencies and Synagogues in Jacksonville. The Foundation
professionally administers lifetime and testamentary giving plans designed to:

¢ Assist individuals to achieve their personal charitable goals in the most tax-

advantaged manner.

* Accumulate enduring endowed resources for use in supporting special,
emergency, and future needs, including those not provided for by the Jacksonville

Jewish Federation’s annual campaign.

The Foundation exists as a partnership of Jacksonville’s Synagogues and
Agencies to assure a better future for all generations. Through the Foundation,
donors are provided with many ways to perpetuate their charitable interests through

a wide array of funding opportunities.

Sol Zim

“America’s Superstar of Jewish Music”
sunday, February 18

An enthusiastic audience welcomed Sol Zim, a Master-Cantor who
electrified the audience with his beautiful tenor voice as he presented Yiddish
and Israeli folks songs, as well as operatic arias and Broadway show tunes.
His award winning songs have been acclaimed as “a key to continued Jewish
culture.” It was a joy to listen to his inspiring performance.The evening
featured a special perfomance by the Solomon Schechter Day School choir
under the direction of Cantor Aron Heller.

Catskill Frolics I
starring Vic Arnell & Holly Lipton

Sunday, January 21

Hillarious comic Vic Arnell,
and talented singer Holly Lipton
provided merriment and music that
truly made the Catskill Mountains
experience uniorgettable. This
husband and wife team brought joy
and pleasure to a receptive audience.
Vic Arnell is the funny friend who
kept them laughing. Holly Lipton
made love songs more intense and a
lullaby more tender. You enjoyed
their last visit to Jacksonville, aren’t
you glad we brought them back?

Jacksonville
Jewish Center

Centennial

Celebration
Toot 28 Dood

The Cub Scouts of Park 14 have been very busy here at
the Center!

In the fall, the Pack, along with a record-breaking number
of enthusiastic parents and siblings, camped out at Ocean Pond
in Osceola National Park. A forest ranger taught the boys about
trees and animals in the forest. They also enjoyed swimming,
hiking, learning to whittle and playing “mad libs.” Everyone
was treated to a Pack 14-style bonfire.

In March, Kevin Norton, Charlie Rait and Steven Lewis
took top honors at the annual Pinewood Derby held at River
Garden. Later in the spring, the Pack revisited Suwanee River
State Park for more canoeing, hiking and camping with their
families.

At Den meetings, the Cubs honed their outdoor skills,
leadership and citizenship abilities, and learned about tzedakah.
Pack meetings included a Hanukkah celebration.

Of course, all of this was made possible by the
commitment of time and energy of all the Pack 14 parents!
A big THANK YOU to Elyssa Vining and Kim Gartner.
Both “retired” this year as den leaders.

They will be missed. We appreciate the contributions
of our den leaders Rose & Larry Hecht, Jerry Schwartz,
Amir Wind and Missy Frisch. Pack 14 is now the proud
owner of its own race track built by Kevin Garten and
myself. Scott Phillips was a great Pinewood Derby
timekeeping, using the most advanced computer technology
to make our race the most accurate anywhere.

With all this enthusiasm, anything is possible for our
scouts!

Bruce Goldring,

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial

Celebration
1901

Our Centennial celebration year brings many
exciting new changes to the Jacksonville
Jewish Center. These changes are the result of
the coordinated efforts of the many dedicated
people who strive to bring our “Initiative for
Excellence” to every facet of the Jacksonville
Jewish Center.

One of our greatest challenges has been met as
we have completed an extensive and arduous
search for new Rabbinical leadership. We are
very fortunate to welcome Rabbi Stephen
Grundfast as our new spiritual leader. His
infusion of new energy and innovative ideas
has created an atmosphere of enthusiasm and excitement. Special
thanks to Jeffrey Morris for his direction and leadership in
chairing the Rabbi Search Committee.

This past year, the Membership Committee, led by Vice President
Phyllis Goldberg, has been divided into four sub-committees in
order to place the greatest emphasis on meeting the needs of our
membership. The sub-committee chairmen, Suzi Weiss (New
Member Development), Janis Fleet (Member Programs and
Development), Jeff and Wendy Sapolsky (Young Family
Programming), and Neil and Bonnie Sandler (Havurot) have been
investing tremendous time, talent, and energy to enhance our
membership services.

The Finance Committee, chaired by Vice President Fred Pozin,
has worked to meet the challenge of financing expanding
synagogue services and programs. The committee has been
faced with balancing additional program requests from members,
educational needs of our schools, and increasing maintenance
needs of our building with traditional funding limitations.

The Education Committee, under
Michael DuBow’s leadership, has
made great strides for our Galinsky
Educational Programs. Michael’s
innovative fundraising techniques,
especially the “IPO”, have provided
our schools with great enhancements
in all areas — technology,
programming, and administration.

 

Michael Shorstein
President

 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

President's Message

 

All of the major committee chairmen, including
Philip Bloom (House), David Schmerer
(Religious), Kathy Osterer (Youth), Etta Drashin
(Adult Education), Beth Shorstein (Mitzvah/
Social Action), Shirley Bielski, “Performing
Artist” and Elyse Whitman (Cemetery) have
expended great effort and energy to upgrade and
enhance their respective areas.

 

The Officers, Committee Chairmen, Executive
Committee and Board Members are committed to
continuing the Jacksonville Jewish Center’s history
of Jewish excellence for all ofits members. Among
the priorities of the coming year are:

We will celebrate our Centennial Anniversary through a series
of special events and dedications. For over a hundred years, the
Jacksonville Jewish Center has created wonderful memories for
its members through the observance of Jewish rituals and
traditions. Moreover, our Synagogue has shown the strongest
commitment to Jewish education. We will have a great
Centennial celebration year that will recognize every aspect of
our lives touched by the Jacksonville Jewish Center.

We will complete our Restoration 2000 project; a refurbishment
campaign to upgrade the facilities of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center to first class condition. We express our sincerest gratitude
to Leonard Setzer who chaired the Restoration 2000 Committee
and also to Philip Bloom who volunteered his services as general
contractor for this project.

We will strive to maximize the involvement of our membership

by reinforcing our strong committee structure. Committees of

our Synagogue are the driving forces, which provide the ideas,

plans and policies for the present and future operations of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center.

We will continue our Initiative for Excellence by
strengthening the communication with members in order
to ensure that the Synagogue continues to be the Center
of our lives. Meeting the needs and expectations of our
membership can only be obtained through effective
communication. Our goal is to continue to foster such
communication with all members so that we understand
and meet their needs and expectations.

In partnership with our members, the Board of Directors
looks forward to an extraordinary year. On behalf of
the Officers, Executive Committee and Board, and all

ee §=who volunteer and work to make the Jacksonville Jewish Center exceed your

 

Year.

expectations, we wish you L’Shanah Tovah T’ikatavu.

A special thanks to Raymond Cohen, Janis Dorman and all of the Yearbook staff
and volunteers for another excellent yearbook.

Robin, Mathew, Benay, and I wish you a healthy, happy and prosperous New

— Michael A. Shorstein

Religious Schools

 

Jewish Center Afternoon Hebrew School

Celebration
190% >." 2001
ERS Ea

Chava Ortner - Principal

The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is designed for students in grades 3-7, and provides an
elementary education leading to Bar/Bat Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.

Meeting on Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays, “the basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on Hebrew
reading, Jewish social studies, and current events relating to Israel. Synagogue skills, holiday observances and knowledge of
prayers are all part of the comprehensive Afternoon Hebrew School program.

Jewish Family & Community Services
3601 Cardinal Point Drive
Jacksonville, FL 32257-5582 ¢ Phone 448-1933
Iris T. Young, Executive Director

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial

Celebration
Loot. opt

Adopt-A-Senior
You can help support Kosher Nutrition, and the elderly in our community who rely
on the program, by “adopting” a senior. Call 448-1933 to learn more.

Adoption

JFCS continues to place babies into loving homes across the country, including
Florida, Connecticut and New York — three states that require a license to place
children. Last year, we found adoptive families for approximately 90 babies.

Bus Rental

Now the community can rent the JFCS buses to shuttle guests to and from life cycle
events and family gatherings. Enjoy bar and bat mitzvahs, weddings and other special
occasions without the headache of coordinating rides for out-of-town guests.

Catering Service

With so much experience preparing good food, JFCS now caters brunches,
engagement parties, bar and bat mitzvahs and other life cycle events. The kitchen
provides delicious menus, tastefully presented, while observing dietary laws.

Community Kosher Nutrition Program
CKNP continues to provide hot, nutritious, kosher meals to the elderly at Mt. Carmel,
in a Safe and friendly environment.

Counseling

JFCS provides quality mental health care by licensed professionals, at reasonable
rates. Confidentiality is always guaranteed. Services include counseling for grief,
depression, family issues, parent-child conflict, life transitions and much more.

Feed A Needy Neighbor
With donations of non-perishable food items from a concerned community, JFCS
provides emergency groceries to families and individuals experiencing difficult times.

Jewish Healing Network
The Jewish Healing Network reaches out to those who are struggling, ill or dying
by sharing the rich resources within the Jewish tradition.

Senior Transportation
JFCS transports seniors to religious services, doctors appointments, shopping centers
and recreational activities for an affordable fee.

There’s So Much More...
These are just a few of the many services offered at JFCS. For those needs the
agency cannot address, staff is always available to refer you to the appropriate

resource.

Home Is Where The Heart Is

Mount Carmel Gardens apartments
was designed, even to the smallest detail,
to provide comfortable and pleasant
surroundings. From the initial concept,
Mt. Carmel Gardens has strived to create
respectable: living for the elderly
community, providing more than
housing. Mt. Carmel Gardens offers a
17-story building on a beautifully
landscaped site, 24-hour staffing,
community facilities, and planned
programs, all of which were developed
as part of an over-all concept...a concept
of responding to the desires of retirees
for security, comfort, . satcry.
independence and the enrichment of
stimulating social-recreational activities
shared with others.

Mount Carmel Gardens is conve-
niently located, with transportation,
shopping, hospital and doctor’s offices
nearby.

1904 5 Boon

 

2nd Annual JJC Golf Classic

Fundraiser is a Major Success

 

Proceeds to Provide Scholarships

The JJC Golf Classic played December 18th, at the Ponte Vedra Ocean
Course, was not only a great financial success, but a GREAT TIME was had by
all who participated. A sold-out field teed off in glorious weather, on a beautiful
course. Camaraderie was high and the competition was keen. Congratulations to

all.

The credit for this outstanding program goes to the hardworking chairmen
and committee. Additional thanks goes to a great crew of tournament-day
volunteers: Robin Allerding, Allison Bailys, Gayle Bailys, Linda Bloom, Helen
DuBow, Debby Fialkow, Edith Horovitz, Lynn Maiman, Jeanine Rogozinski,

Suzi Weiss and Lynn Zimmerman.

 

The Horty T: Gendzier Cup was presented by Scott
Allerding, Tournament Chairman (ctr) to the tournament
winners (1 to r) Terry Jaymes, Brian Kelly, Lex Staley
and Jim Kennedy with Bruce Horovitz (r).

American Red Magen David
for Israe

Magen David Adom has evolved into Israel’s
emergency medical, disaster, ambulance and healthcare
network. 365 days a year, 24 hours a day, every person
in every corner of Israel looks to MDA to perform the
usual tasks carried out by Red Cross Societies throughout
the world, and then some. Within minutes, MDA’s rescue
units arrive on the scene — for medical emergencies,
accidents and, unfortunately, terrorist bombings.

Trained paramedics administer immediate help
and then transport the patient to the hospital if necessary,
Unfortunately they have been very busy this past year,
and there doesn’t seem to be any diminution in tragedies.

Mitzvah Chapter’s Annual Raffle proceeds help
support a cardiac ambulance for the city of Ashdod. Our
Concert at the Cummer has raised funds to keep thos
ambulances running. With 59 ambulances damaged or
destroyed, there’s an unprecedented need for new ones.
Donations in any amount are urgently needed.

Show your support for the State of Israel for
only $25 and do the mitzvah of pikkuach nefesh by
joining today.

Mail to Hana Schnidler, 9830 Woodrose Lane,
Jacksonville, Fl 32257.

‘For us it’s only a check, for them it could mean
life itself.”’

_ Brandeis University ~
National Women’s Committee

The mission of the Brandeis University National
Women’s Committee is to provide financial support and
growth for the Brandeis University Libraries, which
serve a community of students and scholars, in
education and research, united by their commitment to
the pursuit of knowledge. The National Women’s
Committee offers its members opportunity for
intellectual pursuit, continuing education, community
service, social interaction, personal enrichment, and
leadership development. The members act as emissaries
to support and enhance the image of Brandeis, a Jewish-
sponsored, non-sectarian university where excellence
is the tradition.

For more information, call Betsy Pearl, 645-5410.

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial
Celebration
1OOt = BOO
ae ee

One . hundred . years: ~ ae.
approximately 40 Jacksonville families
joimed jorces to micet tie tieeds OF a
growing number of newly arriving Jewish
immigrants. Their solution, in the fall of
1901, was the formation of Congregation
B’Nai Israel, the forerunner of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center.

Could these forty families possibly
have imagined what the next 100 years of Jewish life
would be like in Jacksonville? Could they have possibly
comprehended the impact this new synagogue would
have on future generations? Could they have even
fathomed our programming and facilities as they
exist today?

As we.celebrate this miléstenme of our
congregation’s Centennial our hopes and visions should
be aimed at the next 100 years. What kind of Jewish life
will exist in our community? What will be the role of
the Jacksonville Jewish Center?

 

 

Bruce Horovitz
Executive Director

Executive Director's Message

 

With the observance of our
Centennial year, we have the unique
opportunity to help set the foundation for
this future.

How appropriate that we enter this
year with such great appreciation of our
past and such great optimism for the
future. We begin this next chapter witha
new Rabbi, new professionals in our
youth and education departments and many new
members. Our facility is in the midst of a major
restoration and we continue with significant
enhancements to our Galinsky Educational programs

This coming year will be one of celebration and
opportunity. It is my hope and prayer that each
congregant will take advantage of this extraordinary time
at the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Become involved in
the life of our congregation. Make this year, 5762, one
of renewed commitment and spirituality. Join a
committee; make a minyan; attend a Shabbaton; coach
a basketball team; celebrate Shabbat; support our Golf
Tournament, Raffle and Yearbook; enjoy our recreational
park; participate in Men’s Club and Sisterhood; and
support our Youth groups. There are no limits to your
involvement.

What will the next 100 years be like? We will begin
to answer that question this year!

On behalf of Edith, Sam and Max, best wishes
for a Happy and Healthy New Year.

— Bruce

Center Men’s Club

The Jacksonville Jewish Center Men’s Club is a committed organization

dedicated to the enrichment of Center life and the Jacksonville Jewish Community.
The Men’s Club provides an opportunity for our Center men to work together
supporting, sponsoring and participating in programs that bring meaning to our
youth, companionship to our elders, and involvement in our Jacksonville Jewish
community.

 

an international organization dedicated to the ideals, philosophy and traditions of Conservative
Judaism. Through the support of the Federation we distribute hundreds of Yellow Holocaust
Memorial candles every Yom Hashoah to our Congregation families. This year we will be continuing
the successful FJMC “Hearing Men’s Voices” program; a series of workshops dedicated to creating
a forum for discussion and sharing issues relating to being a Jewish man in today’s world. These
workshops will cover family, religion, society and health in thought provoking and fulfilling agendas
led by leading experts and professionals.

We are committed to our Center youth with award winning programs like the Yad Shel
Chai (Hand of Life) award that rewards our youth for reading Torah, The Youth Achievement
Award for outstanding Confirmation students and presentation of a book to every Bar and Bat
Mitzvah. We also support the Center youth organizations by helping out with conventions and
Supplemental School programs and by sponsoring a sports banquet that brings area sports celebrities to the JJC to talk about
how athletics can help every child “Reach Their Dreams.”

 

The Mens Club Horty T. Gendzier Summer Scholarship fund provides the opportunity for needy children to attend
Israel and USY summer programs and Camp Ramah Darom honoring the memory of Horty Gendzier who was so instrumental
in the pioneering of these programs. Hundreds attend our annual “Man of the Year” Dinner Roast which provides the base
funding for the Horty Gendzier scholarships. These successful roasts honor a JJC Mens Club member for his contribution to

the club and to the Center in an unforgettably funny evening tailored to the uniqueness of the Honoree.

We support the Jacksonville Jewish Federation and the Jacksonville Family and Counseling Service by Tzedakah

programs and are involved with the community at large by volunteering on
Christmas to allow our friends of other faiths to celebrate their holiday with
their families.

We are visible friends of our Center as well with programs like selling
and building Sukkot for our Center families and helping to decorate the Center’s
Goldman Sukkah. You can find Men’s Club members at the Lag B’ omer Picnic
every year selling hot dogs and cokes and you will find us ushering at services
every Shabbat and Holiday. Men’s Club members sponsor, lead and participate
in Men’s Club Shabbat and take an active role in preparing B’nai Mitzvah
students of all ages by sponsoring events and providing tutors and assistance.

These events have earned your Men’s Club First Place and Honorable
Mention Torch Awards from the Federation of Jewish Men’s Clubs in years
past and we are actively pursuing new Torch Awards for community service
and other events.

The Men’s Club is also a great way for friends to have fun. In the fall
we ‘kick off’ our new year with a membership drive party featuring games of
chance and raffles while we watch a Jacksonville Jaguars away game on a
BIG screen TV. In the spring we take our families with us to hockey games
and a Jacksonville Suns baseball game and every summer we unite for the
infamous deep sea fishing trip.

All this and more is waiting you if you are at least 18, male and a
member of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Join now, we need your help!
— Dave

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial

Celebration
1901 2001

Our second Annual
Man of the Year Honoree
was Jeff Morris. Jeff was
treated to merciless kidding
from his family and friends as he was put
on ‘trial’ in a real Court built specially for
the occasion and forced to defend himself
to a jury of his peers. The feeling all along
was that Jeff was a true Mensch, a real gem
who represents the absolute best of what it
means to be a Jew. Always the first to
welcome new members into his home and a
tireless worker for the Center as Financial,
VP, Past President of the Center, Chairman

of the Mens Club, Board member, Jeff Morris set a standard

of leadership that may never be equaled.

It was the task of the prosecutor and Judge (the same person,
Judge Jack Schemer) to prove otherwise and we did so by

wees
Uy
Le

E —pasketball Court a

 

Randall Smith and David Schmerer accept award at
national meeting

34

Organizations

 

bringing witness after witness from Jeff’s life
including his High School Basketball Coach
and teammates from his championship
Wolfson High Basketball team. There was
also video testimony from a former
‘girlfriend’, Judge Schemer even got Jeff’s
Mom, Sonya Morris to testify against him!
It didn’t matter as Jeff was found innocent
and earned the accolades from the audience
that he so richly deserves.

 

Last Year Man of the Year Presents
the this year s award to Jeff Morris

Fun was had by all with good food, another

beautiful room set up by Ellen Rubens and
a Courtroom set built by Richard Ford and the Center
maintenance staff. All proceeds from the evening went to
the Mens Club Horty T. Gendzier Summer Scholarship fund
for needy Jewish Children to attend Camp Ramah Darom
and USY Pilgrimages to Israel and Europe.

 

JJC Men’s Club Wins Torch Award

The Mens Club Yad Shel Chai Program was awarded a First Place
Torch Award for Youth Activities at the Federation of Jewish Mens Clubs
International Convention in Toronto, Ontario, Canada this Summer. This
is the second First Place Torch Award for our Club having received one
for the New Americans B’Nai Mitzvah in 1996. We also received an
Honorable Mention Award in 1997 for our Armed Forces Shabbat

The Men’s Club instituted the very successful Yad Shel Chai (Hand
of Life) award program to encourage and reward post Bar/Bat Mitzvahs
who continue reading Torah on Shabbat, holidays, minyan, at River
Garden and other Center sponsored and supervised events. Teens who
read a minimum of 18 (chai) portions by age 18 are awarded a beautiful,
inscribed Torah pointer (yad) and a certificate. Eighteen teens have
already received this award, and many more are currently enrolled in the
program. We are extremely proud of our Yad recipients and hope to see

" many more achieve this high honor. If you would like more information

regarding this program, please contact Randall Smith or Jim Richman.
===== PAGE 81 =====
L'Shanah Tovah u Metuhah

The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs

:
;

 

Early Childhood

Jacksonville
Jewish Center

Centennial

Celebration
1901 - 2001

The Early Childhood Department of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is
designed to nurture the inquisitive, outgoing spirit in our children. We help
them to be happy with themselves and others, to discover and to grow.
Meeting the emotional, educational and physical needs of each child is
central to the goals of the Early Childhood Department. Our aim is to
develop a positive attitude toward school that will continue into the
elementary years.

 

SS

Dale Schemer This year our Preschool went through the re-accreditation process with the
ees Florida Kindergarten Council. We have once again received a passing report
filled with outstanding praise from the accreditation committee. We are
proud of the fact that we have continuously maintained our accreditation since 1986.

The FKC committee members reported that our staff was “qualified, friendly, cohesive and dedicated to the
well being of the students. Children as well as parents were very happy with the Preschool as evidenced at the
drop-off and pick-up time.” In addition, they reported that the Preschool should be “commended for an
outstanding Judaic and Computer Science Program.”

Our school and extended day program are committed to excellence in education and childcare. We are proud
of our dedicated and loving staff that provide a challenging and stimulating educational environment in which

children have the opportunity to grow and reach their full potential.

We look forward to the 2001-2002 school year and the opportunity to once again provide our students with the
very best preschool and extended day experience.

— Dale Schemer

 

Shirley Thacker

===== PAGE 87 =====
Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial
Celebration
1901 = 2OO1

1950 PHILIP SELBER ELECTED PRESIDENT
At the annual meeting, January 16, 1950, Philip Selber
was elected president. In seconding the nomination,
past president Joseph Hackel commented that “for the
first time in its history, the Jacksonville Jewish Center
calls on a young man born in the city and given his
religious training at the Center, to head the organization.”
Philip Selber served as president for three terms and
continues to be a strong advocate for the Center.

1961 RABBI MOSHE GOLDBLUM

Rabbi Moshe V. Goldblum accepted the position as
rabbi of our congregation. Rabbi Goldblum impressed
everyone with his warm sincerety and genuine devotion.
He imbued those with whom he came in contact with a
new spirit of understanding and dedication to the
Center’s purpose. One of his greatest achievements, with
his wife Evelyn, and a group of dedicated congregants,
was the creation of a Foundation School. These efforts
evolved into the Solomon Schechter Day School.

1963 SAN JOSE BLVD. PROPERTY PURCHASED
With an eye to the future, property at 10101 San Jose
Boulevard in Mandarin was acquired in November 1963.
The next summer a campsite with an Olympic size
swimming pool and playing fields were ready for the
Day Camp.

1972 THE RABBI DAVID GAFFNEY YEARS

The board of directors of the Jacksonville Jewish Center
announced the appointment of Rabbi David Gaffney as
the spiritual leader of the congregation. He arrived with
his wife Inge and their two children, Asher and Shalva.
This was the beginning of a 29 year journey of
inspiration and continuing accomplishments that would
propel our congregation to the forefront of the
Conservative movement.

1973 GROUDBREAKING FOR NEW FACILITY
Groundbreaking for the new synagogue-center complex
was scheduled for September 16, 1973.

1976 CARAVAN OF TORAHS

On Sunday, January 11, 1976, a caravan of automobiles
followed an open truck upon which Center dignitaries
Sat carrying our priceless Torahs from the Ark at 3rd
and Silver to their new home at the new Center site in

A Centennial Chronicle

 

1950 - 2001

Mandarin. It was an historic event which culminated in
a stirring dedication ceremony. This was the beginning
of our present Synagogue Center.

1980 RABBI DOV KENTOF JOINS THE CENTER
As director of education and youth over the past 20 years,
thousands of the children of our congregation, and
throughout the Southeast, have flourished Jewishly
through Rabbi Dov Kentof’s innovative programs,
unique educational style and genuine concern for the
individual. He has drawn in the fringes of our
community like the corners of his own talit instilling a
sense of belonging.

1989 - NEW EXPANSION

To keep pace with the demands for space from our three
growing school programs and the need for more meeting
room space, our magnificent synagogue building would
see many additions, improvements and renovations. One
of most striking additions was the beautiful Ark and
majestic sculpture designed by Israeli artist, Ami Shamir.
Under his direction the ark was erected in time for the
High Holidays, 5743. This magnificent structure has
added an awe-inspiring and elegant quality to our
Sanctuary.

RESTORATION 2000

Currently, the Restoration 2000 project is in full swing,
beautifying the prime areas in preparation for the
Centennial Celebration in the fall of 2001. The proposed
designs emphasize a color scheme that is subtle and
blends with the sanctuary. The variations of pattern and
texture will define the different rooms Many of these
renovations are apparent today as you walk through the
promenade or visit the social hall and the auditorium.

2001- THE CENTENNIAL CELEBRATION

All of the planning and the restoration will be complete
and will culminate in a fabulous Centennial Celebration
in December 2001. It is therefore fitting that we thank
those people who have made this celebration possible.

Note: Copies of Philip Selber’s personal
History of the Jacksonville Jewish Center are
available at the Center office at no charge.

The Restoration 2000 campaign was initiated last year with the goal of restoring our facility to a
first class standard for the 21st century. This exciting and innovative project is on schedule to be
completed, in large measure, in time for the Center’s Centennial Celebration in December 2001.
A newly restored lobby, social hall and auditorium are major components of the Restoration
2000 project, which also includes new
skylights, wall coverings and much Du Bow Family
needed structural repairs. |
This project was made possible by
the generosity of the Patrons featured
on these pages. We are very grateful
for their support and for the work
of the Restoration 2000 design
committee for making this campaign
such a success.

Leonard Setzer - Chairman

1929 RABBI
HARRY COHEN
APPOINTED:
Early in 1929 Dr.
Harry Cohen was
engaged as rabbi. Dr. Cohen, the holder of a PhD, was
ordained by the Jewish Theological Seminary and was
recognized as one of the outstanding scholars of the
rabbinate.

1932 RABBI MORRIS D. MARGOLIS

With the election Rabbi Margolis, the programs of the
Center entered a new growth in its religious and social
activities. Rabbi Margolis was not only rabbi but also
performed the duties of cantor, principal of the schools
and a teacher in the classroom as well. Rabbi Margolis
introduced the first Junior Congregation composed of
the Hebrew School Students, who held their own
services on Shabbat and holidays.

1944 THE THE POST WAR ERA

Harry Gendzier was elected president of the Center in
February of 1944. It was the beginning of dynamic
period of expansion of the Center’s existing programs
and the introduction of new and exciting programs to
enhance the Jewish Center idea. It was through his
leadership that the Jacksonville Jewish Center expanded
its facilities to fit the needs of a growing congregation.
Throughout his tenure, he was a driving force in creating
a true Community Center. In the September issue of
the Center Yearbook, President Gendzier said
“regardless of what community program might come
into being, we at the Jewish Center are firmly resolved
to achieve and develop the finest program for the
building of a knowing, proud and positive Jewish Youth.”

1946 CANTOR MARTON ARRIVES

This was the beginning of an era of a span of more than
43 years. Cantor Marton introduced liturgical music
that is still the benchmark of all services for Shabbat
and all of the holidays. Our children, at their Bar

1929 -

 

 

A Centennial Chronicle

 

1947

Mitzvah, chant the Musaf Service singing prayers as
taught by Cantor Marton even to this day. His legacy of
music has become the standard for our congregation.
One of Cantor Marton’s favorite achievements was the
Center Choral Society, which still provides beautiful
religious music for the High Holidays. In addition to its
participation in services, the Choral Society presented
annual concerts each year featuring nationally known
Cantors. The members have changed over the years, but
Cantor Marton’s influence is still apparent as the voices
sing music he introduced.

1947 - 1960 RABBI SANDERS TOFIELD YEARS
Rabbi Tofield made an indelible mark on our
congregation with his experience and knowledge of
every facet of Synagogue affairs. His wealth of Jewish
knowledge played a large part in the development of
the Center into the tremendous institution that it became.
He was recognized as one of the outstanding scholars
of the Conservative movement. Because of his position
and the resources that he had
to offer, he was able to serve
as a pipeline to bring the
Jewish heritage of the past
into the current activities of
the synagogue.
1947 TED GROSS
ARRIVES

In September 1947, Mr.
Gross came to Jacksonville
to be the Education Director
| of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center and for the next 50 years he devoted his life to
the religious education of our youth as teacher and
mentor. He nurtured a faithful reading of the Torah text
to a legion of Bar and Bat Mitvahs. Through his efforts
the Center has a skilled cadre of Torah readers who read
on Shabbat and the Holidays.

1950 EXPANSION BEGINS

On Sunday, January 8, 1950 groundbreaking ceremonies
were held. By 1959, the impressive campus of three large
buildings housed a two-story main sanctuary complete
with balcony and choir lofts, a chapel, library, social
hall, modern school and playground, state of the art
auditorium/gymnasium, banquet kitchen, spacious
bridal lounge, meeting rooms and offices. -

Center Youth Groups

‘

Jacksonville

Centennial Chalutzim - Grades 4 and 5

Celebration
1901) “a LaOud
eae es

Research has proven that the survival of Judaism depends on the exposure of our youth to Jewish activities, friends and
experiences that commit them to perpetuating that feeling of Jewishness and Jewish life.

The Jacksonville Jewish Center sponsors three outstanding youth groups for youngsters in grades 4-12. Each group
meets regularly and enjoys programs of a religious, cultural and social nature.

Through active participation in these groups, a sense of pride and an identification with Judaism are instilled. Jewish
values, attitude and behavior patterns are discussed and carried out through Mitzvah programs and study.

Conventions, regional activities and camps give our youth the opportunity to meet other Jewish youth from all over the
United States.

The youth programs are coordinated are supervised by the Youth Commission. All groups are affiliated with the Southeast
Region and United Synagogue of America.

2001-2002

Special School Events

 
 

 

jewshcener Consecration 5761 SSDS Seventh Grade Graduation
eee February 3, 2001 May 24, 2001

The Consecration of the First Grade classes of the Solomon
Schechter Day School and the Aleph Class of the Afternoon Hebrew
School, part of the Galinsky Educational Programs was celebrated
during Shabbat morning services, February 3, 2001. Students
demonstrated their knowledge and budding devotion to Judaism in a
timely program about Shalom — Peace.

 

Seventh grade students demonstrated their learning,
their devotion, and their commitment, through a moving
program which they prepared for this special occasion.

 

First Grade A: Mrs. Bonnie Loeser, Hebrew Teacher- Robin Included were examples of the mitzvah projects they
Morris. First Row L to R- Harrison Phillips, Jonah Kitay, Nikki performed to demostrate their understanding of Biblical
Bailys, Rachel Whitman, Michelle Taito. Second Row L to R- commandments. (lst row L to R)Hallie Morris, Omer
Tobi Rudoltz, Zachary Sandler, Rivka Pearlstein, Laura Spalter, Kirill Leonov, Andrew Vining. (2nd row L to R)
Goldman,Dor Eitan Spalter. Third Row L to R- Sam Goodman, Michael Epstein, Jonathan Mizrahi, Jeremy Bailys, Daniel

Rebecca Cooper, Rachel Stark, Jake Friedman, David Ferman. Heller. Todah Rabah to their teachers: Edith Horovitz,
amiaianae me ee Chava Ortner, Judy Reppert and Susann Turner.

SSDS Middle School Washington, D.C.
May, 2001

 

 

 

 

First Grade B:Paula Horn, Hebrew Teacher- Ilana Manasse.
First Row L to R-Nicole Ansbacher, Benjamin Gershon,
Rachel Herman, Daniel Wind, Frankie Zimmerman. Second
Row L to R- Danielle Wirsansky, Jeffrey Weiss, Hailey
Gartner, Shira Lanigan, Monica Koren. Third Row L to R-
Simona Altshuler, David Walker, Ian Broudy, Emily Goldman,

Megan Brown.

From Arlington National Cemetery to the White House,
Ford’s Theatre to the Capital Rotunda. The Newseum to the
Metro, the Solomon Schechter Middle School students saw it all
and then some more on their trip to the Nation’s capitol. They
ate in Kosher restaurants, davened in a hotel lobby and visited
the Israeli Embassy. A highlight of the trip was a visit with
Senator Bob Graham, the show “Sheer Madness” at the Kennedy
Performing Arts Center. Next years trip is to New York.

eS.

 

Jacksonville
Jewish Center

Centennial
Celebration

1901 2001
SAS

“R. Ishmael, his son said: He who learns
with a view to teaching, they give him
the opportunity to learn and to teach.
And he who learns with a view to doing,
they give him the opportunity to learn
and to teach, to observe and to do.”

There is an understanding that
comes from study and learning. When
we read, write, discuss, debate and
challenge our minds to higher thoughts,
we atta that special level of
communication and understanding
which develops when members of
groups work together for their common
purpose and goals. There is joy in the
sharing of ideas and mutual satisfaction in accomplishments.

As I complete 23 years of service to the Jacksonville
Jewish Center, I am grateful for the lives I have touched and
to everyone who has touched mine. My mind is flooded with
memories of the children who have passed through my life
here at the Center — many of them now grown with families of
their own. There have beer: so many events, activities, camp
outs, conventions, classes, discussions, field trips, holiday
celebrations . . . all blending together to form a beautiful
tapestry in my mind. We have drunk together from the fountain
of life, together we have strived for the perpetuation of our
Jewish tradition and heritage, and together we have encouraged
the pursuit of education and synagogue/community
involvement.

Through the close connection we have had in the Hebrew
Schools and Youth programs, I feel as though we are family.
Over the years, we have worked together to build more than
programs — we have built human beings. The thought of
separating from all of you for whom I care so deeply is bringing
a profound sense of sadness that is difficult to describe. In the
back of my mind I always realized this day would come. That

 

 

Rabbi Dov Kentof

Director Education / Youth Emeritus

Rabbi Kentof's Message

 

one generation comes as another
generation goes and, like a parent, I
have to let go with the belief I have done
my job well and a prayer that my
teachings will be remembered and
guide my children through tough times
and difficult decisions.

When I look at all the friends I
have made through these years and,
especially when I look at my students
and youth club members, I realize my
labors have born much fruit. I hope and
pray that all the years of diligent work
and effort will further the cause of
Judaism and love for our people as well
as instill deep feelings for this Synagogue.

As I move onto the next stage of my life, I carry great
warmth and appreciation with me for the wonderful feeling
I have from my years with you. I hope the future will bring
you all happiness, fulfillment, and, above all, a commitment
to Jewish education and Jewish living. Remember, the only
assurance we have for our young people to grow into
committed Jews, is through education — both formal and
informal.

I hope you will continue to take advantage of the many
opportunities offered at the Center to enrich your family and
keep them in the fold of Judaism. I hope and pray that God
will continue to guide the decisions of the Center’s leadership
with wisdom as they take this department into new directions
while maintaining the integrity of all we have accomplished
these past 23 years.

Alina joins me in wishing you and yours A Happy,
Sweet, and Prosperous New Year. Thank you all for
everything.

— Rabbi Dov Kentof

River Garden Auxiliary makes things happen...

The Auxiliary is an independent organization that has been serving
the River Garden Hebrew home since its beginnings, in 1922, as the
Ladies Hebrew Sheltering Aid Society.

The Auxiliary gives financial support to the home BUT MORE
IMPORTANILY, the Auxiliary members work together to enhance
the daily life of each and every resident.

The Auxiliary’s mission is to provide funds for ancillary needs and
services to our residents. The Auxiliary provides a dimension of
warmth and significant funds to meet the needs of the residents. We

 

 

Community Agencies

 

David A Stein Jewish Community Alliance
on the Ed Parker Jewish Community Campus

8505 San Jose Blvd. ¢ Jacksonville, FL 32217
Phone: (904) 730-2100 ¢ Fax: (904) 730-2444
www.jcajax.org
www.JaxJewish.org/jca
Myron I. Flagler, Executive Director

The JCA was founded in 1988 by a group of visionary leaders who provided the
leadership needed to transform the site of a former country club into a state-of-the-art
community center. These leaders saw a need to bring Jacksonville’s Jewish community
together and have a strong involvement in the Jewish community. The leaders sought to
create a positive and affirming environment of Jewish culture and heritage. Since the
doors opened in 1988, this has been accomplished through various and sundry programs
for Jews of all ages — from babies to senior adults.

The JCA is proud of its accomplishments over the past thirteen years. It provides
a common meeting ground for the Jewish community for the affiliated or non-affiliated
Jew who just wants to feel connected to Jewish heritage. When there was a flood of
immigrants from the Soviet Union, the JCA became a haven for the New Americans to
learn the language and American customs. The JCA provides many Jewish cultural
experiences. Highlighting the past four years has been the Jewish Book Festival. The
JCA’s Bessie Setzer Frisch auditorium is the venue for films, music and speakers. The
JCA plays an important role through facilitating Holocaust education through speakers
and Youth Services Theatre Department’s productions. The JCA offers a wide range of
high quality programs for people of all ages including: childcare and family programs,
fitness and recreational facilities and activities, as well as Jewish education.

The JCA’s past presidents, Lois Chepnik, Mark Green, Irene Jaffa, Howard J
Korman, David A.Stein and Bruce Warschoff, have had the foresight and dedication to
help create and sustain the JCA through its growth cycles during the past 13 years. It is
these leaders, who have worked so hard to sustain a positive, affirming environment a
Jewish culture and heritage since the doors opened in 1988.

We invite you to become a member of the JCA. A sliding fee scale is available to
make membership affordable to all. Come by for a tour or take part in one of our many
programs - after all - the JCA is WHERE YOU BELONG, Shalom.

River Garden Auxiliary

With grateful appreciation to
Philip Selber, whose

History of the Jacksonville
Jewish Center was an invaluable
resource of information.

 

Jacksonville
Jewish Center

Centennial
Celebration
190 2001

In the beginning there were five Orthodox Jewish
families in Jacksonville who believed an Orthodox
congregation could be organized to accommodate their
religious needs. At first they met only on the High
Holidays in someone’s home. As their numbers grew,
services were held in the hall of the Masonic Temple.

IT WAS 1901:

By 1901 the number of Orthodox Families had grown
to about forty and they felt it was time to build a real
congregation. With this in mind they took the first step
and that was to legally incorporate. A charter of
incorporation was filed in the Circuit Court and was
approved by Judge R. M. Call on December 5, 1901.
The original, as it appeared on the Charter was “The
Hebrew Orthodox Congregation B’Nai Isarel. It was
later changed to Congregation B’ Nai Israel.

The names of the incorporators listed on the Charter
were among some of the most prominent Jews and
leaders in the history of our congregation. Their names
are familiar to you and many of their descendants are
members of today’s Jacksonville Jewish Center. Such
names as Max Frank, Samuel Cantrovitz (Robert Cantor,
Myra Cantor Cohen), E.H. Pilton (Margo Ruby’s great
grandfather), Morris Wexler, Alex Ossinsky, and Louis
Rothstein were among the incorporators. The first
officers of the new congregation were Max Frank,
president, Samuel Cantrovitz, vice-president, Louis
Rothstein, secretary, Alex Ossinsky, treasurer, and Elias
H. Pilton, Morris Wexler and A. Hirsch, trustees.

IT WAS 1902:

In 1902, now that a congregation was officially formed,
it became obvious that a “Rav” was the next priority. In
addition to leading services, the job description was a
perfect fit for Rev. Benjamin Safer. Rev. Safer was
proficient as a Cantor, baal koreah (Torah Reader), and
a teacher. He was an experienced mohel and shochet
(naturally he had to know which skill was needed for
which purpose). With the financial aid of the
congregation, Rev. Safer established a kosher meat
market where his skill as a shochet was a priority.

With a growing Jewish Community came the need of a
Hebrew School to educate the children and prepare them
to participate in services and ready them for Bar
Mitzvah. The school was a separate institution as was

A Centennial Chronicle

 

1901 - 1906

typical of the European “chedar”. Classes were taught
by the Rev. Safer in his own home or homes of some of
the members of the congregation.

BY 1905:

With the increase in members the problems of how to
create the needed infrastructure for a congregation
became apparent. The obvious needs were for an
Orthodox cemetery, a synagogue building, and school
facility. On July 10, 1905, for the sum of $1000, the
congregation purchased a two-acre site from the
Jacksonville Cemetery Association. This site is known
as the Old Cemetery.

At this same time the congregation took its first step to
erect a building to provide its religious and educational
activities. On July 24, 1905 land was purchased on the
corner of Jefferson and Duval, in Lavilla. The site was
selected because most of the members lived in the
immediate neighborhood. It has been told that the
congregation had a total of $50 on hand to apply to the
purchase price. A portion of the lot was sold to Harry
Goldman, one of the influential leaders in the
development of the congregation. A successful

campaign was launched to raise the $25,000 needed for
the construction. Much of the financial help came from
Jews and non-Jews in the community, as well as Jews
from outside the city. The Winkle brothers of Savannah
donated a carload of lumber. M.J. Weinkle later moved
to Jacksonvilie and became a member of the
congregation.

Jacksonville
Jewish Center

Centennial

Saae Confirmation
Celebrated 6 & 7 Sivan 5760 ¢ May 27-29, 2001

The Biblical festival of Shavuot commemorates the giving of the Torah and Ten Commandments to the
Jewish people. It is natural that this festival should be celebrated with an accompanying sense of commitment to
Jewish life that Confirmation represents. Confirmands demonstrate the knowledge gained through the completion
of our Hebrew High program by full participation in Shavuot services. In addition, this class read essays they
had prepared on major events and people in the 100 Year History of the Jacksonville Jewish Center.

About the Cover:

A 100 YEAR JOURNEY TO CROWN POINT ROAD:
An interpretive painting by Raymond Cohen

The painting is a panorama describing in graphic detail

the growth of our congregation from a modest beginning
to a nationally recognized Synagogue Center. The
illustration is interspersed with vignettes of important |
people, structures and events that marked the development
of the congregation over these 100 years.

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial

Celebration
1901.2.) Dood

The Hebrew poet and
thinker Judah Ha-Levi wrote of his
love for Israel poetically when he
said —’ lee’ bee ba-mizrach wv’ anee
b’maarav” —’my heart is in the East
though I find myself in the West. I
thought of Ha-Levi’s statement as
I sat down to fashion words of holi-
day greeting to the Jacksonville Jew-
ish Center family on the eve of Rosh
Hashanah 5762. For Inge and myself, though we find
ourselves in New York and in close proximity to
children, grandchildren and family, when we reminisce
of happy moments with wonderful friends; when we
review fulfilling achievements and when we consider the
company of dear and precious people —it is then that
we Say so often —’our heart is, in so many ways, still in
Jacksonville.”

This year, 5762, marks a special year for the
Jewish Center family as it celebrates its centennial —100
years of service and devotion to the Jewish community
of Jacksonville and beyond. There are many communities;
there are many congregations, but none quite as special
and unique in its warmth as the Jacksonville Jewish Center.
Having spent the greatest part of our lives and my
rabbinic career in Jacksonville, having shared with you,
dear friends, a great part of the 100 years you celebrate,
I can attest first hand the proud tradition you will
certainly carry with you as you begin the next 100 years.

We have made over the years an extraordinary
impact on the lives of countless people. We provided the
resources for the finest Jewish education children could
receive anywhere. We made possible wonderful Jewish
summer experiences for countless young people who
continue to be blessed by the rich Jewish atmosphere in
which they were nurtured. We enriched the lives of our
members with opportunity for Jewish study; we provided
our community experiences with Jewish culture; we
fostered the love for Israel among young and old; we
opened doors to numbers of our family who came from
other lands seeking the advantages and blessings a
Jewish community such as ours could provide. We saw
young people grow up within the walls of our congrega-
tion prepared to assume the responsibilities of leader-
ship as we saw our seasoned leaders continue in their
devotion and commitment to Jewish life. We comforted

 

Rabbi Emeritus David Gaffney

Rabbi Gaffney’s Message

those who were ill and consoled
others in their bereavement.

We have been a congregation
devoted to its religious tradition — a
minyan and service every morning and
every evening of every day of each
year. We have trained so many of our
congregants with the skills to lead
every facet of every service. There is
no question in my mind that the religious character of
the Jacksonville Jewish community is in great measure
due to the Jewish substance of our congregation.

As I consider the accomplishments of these last
100 years I realize that we are a community of memory.
There is so much of which we as a congregation can be
proud. As we begin the New Year of 5762 we must
recognize that we are also acommunity of hope. We are
a people —not only because of where we have been or
what we presently are. We are a community by what we
choose to become. With the direction of the new spiritual
leadership of Rabbi Grundfast and with the seasoned lay
leadership with which the Center has always been
blessed, I have no doubt but that the future —the next 100
years will be as bright as the last 100 years have been.

Inge joins me in expressing the very best wishes
on this New Year to the entire Center family. We look
forward to seeing you in the very near future as we
celebrate this wonderful Centennial milestone. To para-
phrase Judah Ha-Levi ...our heart is so often with you.

Rabbi David Gaffney

Burial and Mourning

Center Cemetery

The Center owns and maintains two cemeteries adjacent to the Evergreen
Cemetery in North Jacksonville. Both are open daylight hours every day except
Shabbat and Jewish holidays. To reach the Old Cemetery, travel north on North
Main Street to Winona. Make a right on Winona and go until you reach Gate
5. The Old Cemetery is on the left. To
reach the New Cemetery, travel north on
North Main Street to 43rd Street. Make
a right on 43rd Street and the entrance is
at the next right, which is Liberty Street.

We thank the volunteers
who serve on this
important committee:

Elyse Whitman, chairperson
Barbara Cantor
Charlotte Fialkow
Stacey Goldring
Dr. Jeffrey Goldstein
Stuart Hecht
Fred Kupperman
Leonardo Maiman
Morrie Osterer
Marsha Pollock
Nathan Sandler
Blanche Slott
Evan Yegelwel
Seeman Zimmerman

This year, middle school students of
the Solomon Schechter Day School
learned, through the Mitzvah Program,
about the respectful care of the dead,
including tending of burial sites. On a visit
to the Old Cemetery, they discovered that several family plots no longer had
loved ones to maintain them. The students rolled up their sleeves and, with
great care and respect, cleaned the neglected headstones of a family that been
laid to rest more than 50 years ago. We are proud and grateful to these children
for performing an important mitzvah.

 

Students from Solomon Schechter Day
School’s Mitzvah Program cleaned
unattended headstones.

Future plans for the cemetery include improvements to the entrances, as
well as additional landscaping. Contributions can be made to the Cemetery
Fund in honor or in memory of loved ones. All donations will be used to enhance
and maintain our cemeteries.

 

Officers 2000-2001
President
Nathan C. Sandler

VP/Treasurer
Bob Bossen

VP/Education
Ira Grann

Taharah Committee Chairs
Ilse Gottlieb
Sally Becker

VP/Secretary
Naomie Bossen

 

Hevra Kaddisha

It is a source of pride and comfort for the entire Jewish community that
our Hevra Kaddisha is celebrating 30 years of dedicated service to the dear
departed. The burial society presently has 40 active members.

The concept of Hevra Kaddisha is based on kindness — not a reciprocal
type of kindness, but the true kindness of doing and caring for someone who
cannot return the favor. Our members perform these necessary services because
it is the right thing to do. Their satisfaction comes from knowing that they are
helping families at a time of grief and turmoil.

The Hevra Kaddisha is available 24 hours a day to perform the Tahara
(purification) rituals for cleansing and preparing the body for burial; to recite
the traditional prayers and to shroud the body in white linen, Tacrichim; and to
provide a Shomer (watchman) to remain with the body until burial. Families
can take comfort knowing that members of the Hevra Kaddisha are well trained
in the traditional duties, and are devoted to showing the utmost respect for the
deceased.

The Jewish community, regardless of affiliation, 1s encouraged to call
and discuss their concerns with any of our officers, as well as the rabbis.
Dedication 1s our watchword.

—Nathan C. Sandler, president

Sunday School

The SUNDAY SCHOOL of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is
planned expressly for children in kindergarten, first and second grades.
A weekly, two-hour program gives each child the opportunity to
experience the richness of his/her Jewish heritage through song,
dance, role playing, cooking, short stories, games, arts and crafts.
Emphasis is placed on the holidays and festivals. Jewish values and
mitzvot are encouraged. Many thanks to our wonderful Sunday
School teachers Susan Kadish and Susan Neadle.

Religious Schools PTA

 

We are looking forward to another exciting year with

Purim at Sunday School. our Afternoon Hebrew, Sunday School and Beit Midrash
classes.
Youth Congregations Our younger students seem to become more involved
each year with our Jewish Holidays. They love performing in
Pre-Junior Congregation programs for Passover and Purim. Our older students are
Kindergarten-2nd Grade becoming serious, committed Jews.

Meets Saturdays, | la.m.-Noon Parental involvement is so very important in a child’s

religious education. Volunteers are always needed, and we
believe your children benefit from seeing you helping out.
Please feel free to volunteer whenever you are able, showing
your support for our programs.

1901 - 2001

 

 

 

 

11401 Old St. Augustine Road ¢ 260-9020 * www.rivergarden.org

“A Caring Community”

For over 55 years River Garden has met its mission: To meet the unique
residential geriatric needs of the Jewish Community while serving people of all
faiths; To Provide the finest in specialized geriatric rehabilitation and skilled nursing
services to the community at large; To enrich the entire community as a resource
in geriatric careand knowledge; To serve rich and poor alike with caring and
excellence; To create an environment which is supportive of Jewish identity and
informed by Jewish values. Located on a beautiful 35 acre Mandarin campus
containing lush Florida Oak and Pine trees, a private lake, meandering walking
paths,River Garden is the perfect setting for residents and visitors. River Garden
Hebrew Home/Wolfson Health & Aging Center has become the anchor of agrowing
system of elder services including the Home, The Coves, Family CareSupport
Home Health Services, and the Adult Day Program. River Garden is anational
model of «cellence in itsfield.

River Garden’s programs of short-term rehabilitative/respite care, long-term
residential care, Alzheimers’ Dementiacare and Adult Day Care, serve close to
200 people daily. A devoted, professional full time staff of over 230 programs
guide these programs. Staff includes:physicians and beauticians; nurses, social
workers, pharmacist, activities specialists; physical, occupational and speech
therapists; dieticians, etc. In addition, scores of dedicated volunteers help create a
special caring community.

Rver Garden is community where people live, love and care; a community
of many lifestyles and of rich Jewish content, and a community which every day
strives to live up to the mandate of the Fifth Commandment, “Honor thy father

and mother that thy days may be long...”

e Meo =k
Now in its seventh year, this elegant yet
affordable retirement community is located

on River Garden’s 35 acre campus in
Mandarin.

to provide resources for programs and facilities to enhance the quality of life for

provide a full spectrum of residential options.

Center Sisterhood

Jacksonville
Jewish Center
Centennial

Celebration
Logie =) 2ood
(Tes a)

This past year has been one of accomplishment and hard work by our entire Sisterhood team. We
have all made contributions of time and effort in order to accomplish our goals of education, fund
raising and religious observance.

Our monthly program meetings were both entertaining and informative, from skits to speakers to
educational games. We got to know each other better through a people scavenger hunt, and tested

 

2000-2002 Officers

President

Maxine Romo
Education VP

Debbie Banks
Membership VP

Robin Shorstein
Ways & Means VP

Jeanine Rogozinski
Torah Fund VP

Gayle Bailys
Youth VP

Robin Allerding
Treasurer

Joanne Rosenberg
Financial Secretary

Elissa Vining
Recording Secretary

Etta Drashin
Corresponding Sec.

Janis Dorman
Parliamentarian

Bonnie Sandler
Budget

Joanne Rosenberg
Nominating Committee

Beth Shorstein
Administrative Asst.

Shirley Bielski

 

 

 

our Jewish knowledge with our own version of the Millionaire
game. We learned about the Florida nursing home crisis,
and what we could do to help. At our Torah Fund luncheon,
we honored past president Marilyn Garber with the first
annual Horty T. Gendzier Woman of Achievement award, appropriately named for the
woman who contributed so much time and effort to the Torah Fund campaign. We were
mesmerized as Rabbi Eliezer Ben- Yehuda, grandson of the famed Israeli pioneer and
statesman, regaled us with the story of his renowned family. I hope that next year our
programs will again reflect the diverse interests of our members.

Maxine Romo
President

Sisterhood members participated in the Women’s League Biennial convention in
Washington, D.C., with 3 Jacksonville women attending. Barbara Safer was installed as
an international Vice President, and we have 4 Jacksonville women on the International
Board. Four of our members also attended the annual Florida Branch Conference in
Fort Meyers. Our Sisterhood has a Florida Branch Vice President(Phyllis Goldberg) as
well as 4 members on the Branch board.

Our financial support for the religious schools and young people of the Center continued
with our donations to the Youth Fund, Leagrams for Consecration and Confirmation,
scholarships for Camp Ramah, USY on Wheels, and summer programs in Israel. Our
support also included snacks for High Holidays, apples and candy for Simchat Torah,
and hamentaschen for Purim.

Educational and religious programs focused on enlightening monthly seminars led by
Rabbi Gaffney. Our members and their daughters demonstrated their many talents and
abilities during our spiritually uplifting Sisterhood Shabbat and Women’s Minyan. We
were also fortunate to continue with several informative book reviews after Shabbat
services.

Successful fund raising continued with Rosh Hashanah flower and card sales, Nachas

Tax and Donor funds, and our family spring picnic. Please patronize the Sisterhood

Judacia Shop, which benefits all members of the congregation and community with

beautiful gift and ritual items. Look for these activities and others to continue in the
coming year.

The mission of Sisterhood as defined by Women’s League
for Conservative Judaism is “to strengthen and unite
synagogue women’s groups and their members; support them
in mutual efforts to understand and perpetuate Conservative/
Masorti Judaism in the home, synagogue and community;
and reinforce their bonds with Israel and with Jews
worldwide’. In this coming year, let us celebrate the value
of volunteering our services, establishing Jewish homes,
creating Jewish families, and building Jewish communities.

Don and I wish you all a Shana Tovah, a year filled with joy
and peace.

— Maxine

Left to right: Phyllis Goldberg, Barbara Safer, Maxine Romo, and
Beth Shorstein.
